# EXHIBIT G

## PPO Weaponization — Recantation to Filing in 48 Hours

**Case:** Pigors v Watson, Case No. 2024-001507-DC
**Court:** Michigan Supreme Court — Original Jurisdiction
**Filing:** F05 — Application for Superintending Control
**Plaintiff:** Andrew James Pigors, appearing pro se
**Defendant:** Emily A. Watson
**Date Compiled:** April 01, 2026
**Days Since Last Contact with L.D.W.:** 248 days (since July 29, 2025)

---

### PPO Filed Two Days After Recantation

1. **October 13, 2023:** Emily tells police (NSPD-2023-08121): "nothing was physical"
2. **October 15, 2023:** Emily files PPO (Case No. 2023-5907-PP)

The PPO was not filed for legitimate protection — Emily herself told police nothing physical occurred. The PPO was a tactical weapon for custody advantage.

> # PART II — BRIEF IN SUPPORT OF PETITION FOR ORDER OF SUPERINTENDING CONTROL ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
>
> — (01B_BRIEF_IN_SUPPORT.md)

> Every link in this chain traces back to the fraudulently obtained PPO. Under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d), every order in the chain is void and may be vacated at any time. Under MCR 2.612(C)(3), this Court may grant relief from the entire chain through an independent action for fraud upon the court, with no time bar.
>
> — (01B_BRIEF_IN_SUPPORT.md)

### Legal Significance

- MCL 600.2950: PPO requires genuine fear of harm
- Recantation two days before filing negates claimed fear
- Pattern: False report -> PPO -> ex parte custody -> exclusion of Father
